<b>kugang_{1}</b> <i>a</i> @startled. <i>Hastang kugánga nákù
paglagpak sa sira</i>, God! How that slamming

startle, be startled. <i>Nakugang (nakugangan)
ku sa pagbutu sa ribintadur</i>, I was startled
when the firecracker burst. <b>kugangkugang</b>
<i>n</i> <b>1</b> skin eruptions on some parts of the
body of various sizes, thought to be caused
by fear, fright, or being startled. This disease
is usually diagnosed in small children
and the cure is smoke treatment with the <i>kugangkugang</i>
herb. <b>2</b> low-growing, woody
herb of waste places used to treat children
who have the skin eruptions also called <i>kugangkugang</i>.
The <i>kugangkugang</i> is set on
fire just after sundown, and the child is
made to inhale the smoke. The treatment
is repeated for three consecutive afternoons.

<b>kulugpus</b> v [AN; c1] 1 fold the arms in any
position with the forearms crossed as a sign
of repose. <i>Nangulyugpus lang siya nga nagpaábut
ug trák</i>, He stood with his arms
folded waiting for the bus. <i>Nagpangulyugpus
sa íyang mga buktun nga nangalíya sa
mahal nga birhin</i>, She prayed to the blessed
Virgin with her arms crossed, hands on the
shoulders. <b>1a</b> curl the legs up close to the
body. <i>Íyang kulugpúsun ang íyang mga tiil
ug tugnawun</i>, He'll curl up his feet if he
feels cold. <b>2</b> do nothing in the face of a
situation which calls for action. <i>Nangulyugpus
lang siya samtang nagkapulíkì mig trabáhu</i>,
He just stood by with his arms folded
while we went crazy with so many things
to do. <i>Magkiyugpus ba lang tang magtan-aw
sa ílang kalisud?</i> Shall we just stand by
utterly indifferent to the situation?

<b>kulukar</b> (not without <i>l</i>) <i>v</i> 1 [AP; c] place

<b>1a</b> [A; c1] find, obtain s.t. for which there
is fierce competition. <i>Kun mag-ulan kúlì

it is difficult to get public transportation.
<b>2</b> [A; c] attend to s.t. so that it is done

was not a single relative to attend to the funeral.
<i>Sa nakulukar na ang minatay nag-áway

<b>kumári</b> <i>n</i> a woman who has one of the following

Aku sad kumári níya,</i> Cordaping is my
<i>kumári</i> on three grounds: she is the mother
of my godson, and of another son whom I
sponsored in marriage, and the mother of
my daughter-in-law. And for that reason I
am also her <i>kumári</i>. <b>a</b> term of address to a
person with whom one has a relation of <i>kumári</i>.
<b>b</b> friendly term of address to a woman
of one's own generation with whom one is
familiar. <i>Short form:</i> <b>mari</b>. <i>Kumusta mari?</i>

<b>kumbinasiyun</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> combination of things that

ang pagadur ug magpatantu ka sa impliyádu</i>,

<b>kumpas_{1}</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> being in harmony or correct

<b>2</b> deliberate, slow, and poised in

kaáyu manlihuklihuk</i>, That girl is very nice;
she moves slowly and gracefully. <i>Kumpas
pinadulut ang íyang sinultihan,</i> She is slow
and careful in speech. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> beat, time. <i>Dílì
ku makaagpas sa kumpas niánang sunatáha</i>,
I cannot catch onto the tempo of that
song. <b>2</b> acts, mannerism. <i>Mu ra man nà siyag
buang sa íyang mga kumpas</i>, She seems
like a mad woman, the way she acts. <b>kuntra
--</b> out of rhythm or tempo. <i>Kuntra kumpas
ang ímung sinayawan</i>, You are not dancing
in time to the music. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AC; c1] act or do
s.t. in harmony or time. <i>Mikumpas siya pagpakpak
uban sa sunáta</i>, She clapped in time
to the music. <i>Nagkumpas ang duha ka bátà
ug singgit</i>, The two children shrieked in
unison. <b>2</b> [B; a] be, become deliberate and
posed in action, cause s.t. to be slow and
deliberate. <i>Mikumpas ang íyang tíngug (mikumpas
siya sa íyang tíngug) sa nasukù na
ku</i>, Her voice became soft and measured as
I grew angrier and angrier. <i>Ug dì ka magkumpas,
mahúlug ka</i>, If you aren't slow and
deliberate, you'll fall. <b>3</b> [C2; b] keep up
with what s.o. else does. <i>Makigkumpas man
gud ning ákung anak ug unsay buhátun sa
mga anak sa dátù</i>, This child of mine wants
to do whatever the rich people's children
do.

<b>kumpas_{2}</b> <i>n</i> compass for determining directions
or for drawing circles.

mayur ang urdinansa anhà pa nà muipiktu</i>,
As soon as the mayor certifies his approval,
the ordinance will take effect. <b>-du</b> <i>a</i> confirmed,
having received the sacrament of
Confirmation. <b>-siyun(->)</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> confirmation
in a religion. <b>2</b> confirmation of an appointment
or ratification of a law.

<b>kumpisal</b> <i>v</i> [A; c] <b>1</b> go to confession. <i>Kinahanglang
mukumpisal úsà mukaláwat</i>, One
should go to confession before taking Holy
Communion. <b>2</b> confess to a crime. <i>Mikumpisal
ra ang mamumúnù</i>, The murderer finally
confessed. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] hear confession.
<i>Túa ang párì sa uspital magpakumpisal
sa mga masakitun</i>, The priest is in the
hospital hearing confession for the patients.
<b>-an(<-), kumpisinaryu, kumpisinaryuhan</b> <i>n</i>
confessional box. <b>paN-, paN-(<-)</b> <i>n</i> act of
confessing in church.[+]

<b>kumpisinaryu see KUMPISAL.</b>

<b>kumpisk[va]r</b> <i>v</i> [A; a2] confiscate. <i>Gikumpisk[va]r
ang tíbi kay wà siya makadata</i>, His <sc>TV</sc>
was confiscated because he didn't keep up
-----File: 1035.png--------------------------------------------------------
the payments. <b>kumpiskádu</b> <i>n</i> s.t. that has
been confiscated. <i>Gibaligyà ang mga sigarilyung
kumpiskádu</i>, They sold the confiscated
cigarettes. <b>kumpiskadur</b> <i>n</i> one whose
job is to confiscate things. <i>v</i> [B156] be, become
a confiscator.

<b>kumpisur</b> <i>n</i> priest who hears confession and
gives absolution.

<b>kumpisyun</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> confession of guilt. <b>2</b> the sacrament
of confession in church. <i>v</i> [A2N; b8][**joined b & 8]
go to confession. <i>Kausa ra ku mukumpisyun
(mangumpisyun) sa usa ka túig</i>, I go
to confession only once a year. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A3; b]
hear confession. <b>-aryu = KUMPISINARYU.</b>
<i>see</i> <b>KUMPISAL.</b>

<b>kumpit_{1}</b> <i>n</i> k.o. full-bodied boat with a deep
draft and without outriggers, wider than
other native boats. They are used for long
distance travel, esp. by Muslims in carrying
on trade. <i>v</i> [A; ac] travel, bring by <i>kumpit</i>.

<b>kumpit_{2}</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] squeeze s.t. between two
long things to hold it. <i>Nagkumpit siya sa
íyang pinangkù</i>, She held her hair bun in
place with a hairclip. <i>Kumpíta pagkúhà ang
inánag mais</i>, Take the roasted corn with
tongs. <i>Ikumpit kining duha ka lipak pagpunit
sa ilagà</i>, Pick up the rat with these two
sticks. <i>Gikumpítan sa asáwa ang láwas sa
bána</i>, The wife held her husband's body
firmly with her legs. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> hairclip. <b>2</b> tongs. <b>3</b>
chopsticks.

<b>kumpitinsiya</b> <i>n</i> competition or competitor.
<i>Mahal ning tindahána kay way kumpitinsiya</i>,
This store is expensive because there are
no competitors. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AC; b] be competing.
<i>Mukumpitinsiya man nímu nang bag-ung
istudiyanti</i>, The new student is going to
give you competition. <i>Sa nigusyu ra sila
nagkakumpitinsiya</i>, They are rivals in business
only. <i>Gikumpitinsiyáhan ang Amirika
sa Rusya sa pag-adtu sa búwan</i>, Russia competed
against America to get to the moon.
<b>2</b> [b] outshine. <i>Nasukù siya kay nakumpitinsiyahan
(nakumpitinsiyaan) man ang bag-u
níyang sinínà</i>, She got mad because s.o.
else outshone her in her new dress.

<b>kumpítis</b> <i>n</i> confetti.

<b>kumpiyansa</b> <i>n</i> confidence in s.o. or oneself.
<i>Wà kuy kumpiyansa sa táwu nga bakákun</i>,
I have no confidence in a liar. a confident.
<i>Napildi siya kay kumpiyansa ra kaáyu</i>, He
lost because he was so over-confident. <i>v</i> <b>1</b>
[A; b] have trust or confidence in oneself
or s.o. <i>Nagkumpiyansa siyang makadaug,
maung wà na magpraktis</i>, He was sure he
could win so he didn't practice. <b>2</b> [A; c]
entrust s.t. to s.o. <i>Makumpiyansahan kahà
nà siyag sikrítu?</i> Do you think we can trust
-----File: 1036.png--------------------------------------------------------
her with a secret? <i>Ayawg ikumpiyansa nang
ímung anak sa míd</i>, Do not entrust your
child to your maid. <b>abúsu di-</b> breach of confidence
or of trust. <i>Ug isugílun nímu ang
sikrítu, kanà abúsu dikumpiyansa</i>, If you
tell the secret, that will be a breach of confidence.
<i>Ang pagkawkaw mu sa sáping gibílin
ku nímu mauy abúsu dikumpiyansa</i>, It
was a breach of trust for you to touch the
money that had been left with you.

<b>kumpli</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> finish with one's service or study.
<i>Ang tanan kung mga bátà kumpli na sa ílang
pagtuun</i>, All my children have completed
their studies now. <b>2</b> completely ruined,
spoiled beyond use. <i>Mau pay pingag ang
pinggan, ímu pung gibuak, kumpli na</i>, The
plate may have been chipped, but it was
still useful. Now you broke it. So that's it.
<b>3</b> all done, finished. <i>Kumpli na ang bayranan
sa balay</i>, My payments on the house
are complete now. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A] finish a term,
one's study. <i>Magpaábut lang ku hangtud
makakumpli ku sa ákung sirbisyu</i>, I'll wait
until I can complete my service. <b>1a</b> [A2; b6][**joined b & 6]
retire from the armed forces. <i>Kapitan
ang ranggung íyang gikumplihan</i>, He retired
a captain. <b>2</b> [a12] be completely ruined
beyond use. <i>Kumplíha na lang nà arun kailisdag
bag-u</i>, Finish it off, why don't you,
so we have to buy a new one. <i>n</i> = <b>KUMPLIANYU.</b>

<b>kumplianyu</b> <i>n</i> birthday. <i>v</i> [A13; b] hold a
birthday party. <i>Káda túig kumplianyúhan
giyud siya sa íyang mga ginikánan</i>, Every
year her parents give her a birthday party.
<b>paN-</b> <i>v</i> [A2] attend a birthday party.

<b>kumplikádu</b> <i>a</i> complicated, difficult to untangle
or understand. <i>Mas kumplikádu ang
makina sa mutursiklu kay sa muturbáyik</i>,
The motorcycle has a more complicated
motor than a motorbike. <i>Kumplikádu ning
kasúha</i>, This is a complicated court case. <i>v</i>
[B1245] be, become complicated.

<b>kumplikar</b> <i>v</i> [B] for a disease to have complications.
<i>Mikumplikar (nakumplikar) ang
íyang plú ngadtus íyang kasingkásing</i>, His
flu developed complications of the heart.
<b>kumplikasiyun</b> <i>n</i> complication in a sickness.

<b>kumplimintu</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> s.t. said or done out of respect
or good manners. <i>Kumplimintu lang
tung íyang pagdápit nímu kay silíngan man
mu</i>, She invited you out of courtesy because
you're her neighbor. <i>Bísan wà nay gustu, gibaslan
ku ang suwat ágig kumplimintu</i>,
Even though I don't like her any more, I
answered her letter for politeness' sake. <b>2</b>
compliment, s.t. said in admiration or
praise. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; b(1)] say or do s.t. insin-*
-----File: 1037.png--------------------------------------------------------
*cere out of politeness. <i>Mukumplimintu lang
kug tambung sa íyang parti</i>, I'll just attend
his party out of courtesy. <b>2</b> [A2] say s.t. in
admiration or praise. <i>Mikumplimintu siya
nakù sa bag-u kung hirdu</i>, She complimented
me on my new hairdo.

<b>kumplín</b> <i>v</i> [A2; c6] complain about one's
grades in school. <i>Kun wà ka mahimuut sa
ímung mga grádu, ngánung dì ka man mukumplin?</i>
If you aren't satisfied with your
grades why don't you complain?

<b>kumplítu</b> <i>a</i> complete, having s.t. complete.
<i>Kumplítu ang iskuyláhan sa mga kasangkápan</i>,
Our school is completely equipped.
<i>Kumplítu ang ákung gamitun sa pamanday</i>,
My tools for carpentry are complete. <i>Kumplítu
ta sa impliyádu</i>, We have our full contingent
of employees. <i>Ang búhat nga kumplítu
ihátag sa maistru</i>, All papers that are
complete should be turned in to the teacher.
<i>v</i> [AB12; a] be, become complete, make
s.t. complete. <i>Mukumplítu kug báyad sa
matrikula</i>, I'll pay the tuition fees in full.
<i>Kining istáma mauy mukumplítu sa ákung
kuliksiyun</i>, This stamp will make my collection
complete. <i>Nagkakumplítu na ang
ngípun sa bátà</i>, The child's teeth are almost
complete. <i>Mu ray ikakumplítu námù ug ma
Pasku</i>, The only time the whole family can
get together is on Christmas.

<b>kumplut</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> conspirator. <i>Ang kahíru usa sa
mga kumplut sa pangílad sa sápì</i>, The cashier
was one of the people who plotted to
swindle the money. <b>2</b> person with whom
one is intimate such that arrangements can
be made on favored terms. <i>Giprumut siya
kay kumplut man sa manidy[vi]r</i>, He was promoted
because he had made especial arrangements
with the manager. <i>v</i> [C] <b>1</b> conspire.
<i>Nakigkumplut ang ismaglir sa pulis sa
pagpalusut sa mga sigarilyung ismágul</i>, The
smuggler connived with the policeman to
let in his smuggled cigarettes. <b>2</b> become intimate
with s.o. to make special illegal arrangements.

<b>kumpra</b> <i>v</i> [AN; a] buy s.t. in quantity, go
shopping. <i>Nakapangumpra ka na bag pára
sa ímung kumbira?</i> Have you bought the
things for your party? <i>Kumpráha ning tanang
nía sa lista</i>, Buy all the things on this
list. n things bought. <i>Unsa may ímung
kumpra?</i> What things did you buy? <b>-dur(->)</b>[**moved up (->)]
<i>n</i> buyer, dealer in some commodity.
<i>Mga kumpradur sa kupras</i>, Dealers in copra.
<i>v</i> [A13] become a dealer. <i>see also</i> <b>MALAPÍ.</b>

<b>kumprumísu</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> committal to s.t. onerous
or objectionable from which there is no
-----File: 1038.png--------------------------------------------------------
turning back. <b>2</b> spouse or family as one's
responsibility. <i>Karun nga may kumprumísu
ka na sa ímung kinabúhì, pagbinuutan na</i>,
Now that you're married, you must resolve
to be good. <i>v</i> [A; a] be committed to such
objectionable situations. <i>Nagkumprumísu
nákù ning pagkapalíta sa awtu kay dì kung
kaabut sa dáta</i>, It put me in a tight fix to
buy this car because I can't meet the installments.
<i>Ayawg paságad ug pirma kay tingálig
makumprumísu ka</i>, Don't sign anything
recklessly. It might get you into hot water.
<i>Nakumprumísu ku pagbúrd sa ákung bátà</i>,
I got myself into debt when my son took
the bar exams.

<b>kumprumitíbu = KUMPRUMITÍDU.</b> <i>see</i> <b>KUMPRUMITIR.</b>

<b>kumprumitir</b> <i>v</i> [A2; c] promise, pledge. <i>Mikumprumitir
ku nga mubáyad sa tápus búlan</i>,
I pledged to pay at the end of the
month. <i>Gikumprumitir na níya ang íyang
kasingkásing sa láing táwu</i>, She has already
pledged her heart to another man. <b>kumprumitídu</b>
<i>a</i> bound, committed to do s.t.

<b>kumprunta</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A2N; c] ask or seek one's
opinion or advice on s.t. <i>Mikumprunta (nangumprunta)
na mig abugádu íning ámung
kásu</i>, We consulted a lawyer about our case.
<i>Ngánung dì man nímu ikumprunta nang
prublimáha sa ímung kumpisur?</i> Why don't
you seek the advice of your father confessor
regarding that problem? <b>2</b> [A; a] sound
s.o. out to see how he feels about s.t. <i>Kumpruntaha
si Tátay ug úyun ba siyang iprinda
ang yútà</i>, Ask father's opinion if he will
go along with mortgaging the land.

<b>kumprunt[va]r</b> <i>v</i> [A12; c] set a timepiece. <i>Ikumprunt[va]r
ang rilu sa radiyu</i>, Set your
watch by the radio.

<b>kumpuni, kumpunir</b> <i>v</i> [A; abc] do make-*shift
repairs. <i>Átù lang ning kumpunihun
kay way bag-ung pyísa</i>, We'll just do make-*shift
repairs because we don't have new
spare parts. <i>Kumpunihan lang ug pasta ang
bangag sa tangu</i>, Just put a temporary filling
in this tooth. <i>Ikumpunir lang ug tápak
ning playwud sa bungbung</i>, Just fix this
wall with a piece of plywood.

<b>kumpurmi 1</b> depending on, in accordance
with. <i>Ang gidak-ung palitun kumpurmi lang
sa sukud</i>, The size to buy depends on her
measurements. <i>'Unsay ákung ihátag nímu?'--'Aw,
kumpurmi lang,'</i> 'What shall I give
you?'--'Oh, it depends on you (whatever
you have).' <b>1a</b> according to what is necessary.
<i>Nanghípus na sila sa ílang mga kumpurmi
lang nga dad-unun</i>, They were packing
whatever it was that they used to take.
-----File: 1039.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>Isigbáyad sila kumpurmi sa ílang nakúhà</i>,
Each one paid according to the amount he
had borrowed. <b>1b</b> whatever happens to be
at hand, whatever comes into the head.
<i>Kumpurmi lay pangayúun ning batáa</i>, This
child asks for whatever enters his head.
<i>Kumpurmi sa íyang makítà íyang palitun</i>,
He buys whatever he sees. <b>1b1</b> different
kinds or sorts. <i>Kumpurmi lang ang ílang gipamalit
sa Karbun</i>, They bought all different
things in the market. <b>1b2 nanimáhung</b>
-- an odor to be so foul that words cannot
describe it (lit. smells like anything and
everything bad). <b>2</b> be in agreement. <i>Bisag
kaáway ta apan kumpurmi ku sa ímung idíya</i>,
We may be enemies, but I agree with
your ideas. <i>Kumpurmi ka ba nga sa Sabadu
na lang ta mangadtu?</i> Is it all right with
you if we go on Saturday instead? <b>3</b> same
as. <i>Unsa ka dakù ang lungag nga tamnan ug
ságing? Kumpurmi sa tamnan ug lubi</i>, How
large a hole do we make for planting bananas?
The same size as the hole for planting
coconut trees. <i>'Pila ka mitrus nga panaptun
ang ímung palitun?'--'Kumpurmi sa imúha,'</i>
'How many meters of cloth will you
buy?'--'The same as what you buy.' <b>4</b>
now look who's talking. <i>'Túa ag kawatan!'--'Kumpurmi
lag kinsay nadakpan,'</i> 'There
you are, you thief!'--'Look who's talking?
Who was arrested, anyway, me or
you?' <i>Unsay dakug káun? Kumpurmig
kinsay nakahurut ug usa ka bandihádu nátù!</i>
What do you mean eating too much!
Look which one of us finished a whole platter
off? v [A12] be agreeable. <i>Ang mga táwu
nga dílì mukumpurmi sa súgù silútan</i>,
Whoever doesn't agree to follow the orders
will be punished. <i>Wà siya mukumpurmi sa
plánu</i>, He was not agreeable to the plan.

<b>kumpurtabli</b> <i>a</i> comfortable. <i>Kumpurtabli
ning síya</i>, This chair is comfortable. <i>Kumpurtabli
ílang kahimtang</i>, They are in comfortable
circumstances. <i>Kumpurtabli ning
sinináa. Dílì hugut, dílì galhà</i>, This is a comfortable
dress. It's not tight, and it's not
hot. <i>v</i> [B2] be comfortable.

<b>kumpúsir</b> <i>n</i> composer. <i>v</i> [B156] become a
composer.

<b>kumpusisyun</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> a musical composition. <i>Ang
átung nasudnung áwit kumpusisyun ni Hulyan
Pilípi</i>, Our national song was composed
by Julian Felipe. <i>2</i> compositon[**composition] book. <b>3</b>
written theme. <i>v</i> [A1] write a composition.

<b>kumpusitur disapátus</b> <i>n</i> shoemaker.

<b>kumpúsu</b> <i>n</i> ballad in a minor key treating of
love or heroism. It is composed of stanzas
of four lines of no set number of syllables
-----File: 1040.png--------------------------------------------------------
and which may have one or two syllables
more than the song allows, but at least two
of which must be rhymed. The melody may
be the same throughout the <i>kumpúsu</i> or
two melodies may be alternate, the second
modulated four notes higher than the initial.
<i>v</i> [A; b6] compose this sort of ballad.

<b>kúmu 1 --</b> [<i>noun, adjective</i>] as one in [such-and-such]
a capacity. <i>Kúmu magulang siya
nímu, mutáhud giyud ka níya</i>, As your older
brother, you must obey him. <i>Kúmu gwápa,
daghang mulíngì iniglabay níya</i>, Being
beautiful, many people turn to look at her
as she passes by. <b>2 -- kay</b> since, seeing that.
<i>Kúmu kay girikumindar kag pulitiku, nakulukar
ka na</i>, Because a politician recommended
you, you got placed in a job. <i>Kúmu
ba kay prisidinti siya sa kapunúngan, dílì
siya muámut?</i> Just because he is the president
of the organization, he doesn't contribute?
<b>3 may, way</b> -- there is s.t. (nothing)
as good as.... <i>May kúmu pa bang basahun
ingun sa Bisayà?</i> Is there any magazine
as good to read as the <i>Bisaya? Way kúmu
ning dúna tay amígu sa Kustum</i>, There's
nothing as good as having a friend in the
Customs Bureau.

<b>kúmù</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> clenched fist. <b>2</b> <i>interjection indicating
a brusque rejection of one's suggestion:</i>
go to hell! <i>'Ikay manghúgas run, ha?'--'Kúmù!'</i>
'You wash the dishes today,
OK?'--'Drop dead, will you?' <i>v</i> [A1N; ac1][**joined ac & 1]
clench one's fist, keep s.t. tightly in
one's palm. <i>Nangúmù siya sa hilabihang kalágut</i>,
He clenched his fists in anger. <i>Kumúa
nang kindi arun dì makítà</i>, Keep the candy
in your fist so that no one can see it. <i>Kumúa
(ikúmù) ang ímung kamut</i>, Clench
your fists. <b>-in- = KÚMÙ</b>, <i>n.</i> <b>-in-ay</b> <i>v</i> [C23]
clench fists at each other.

<b>kumuda, kumúda</b> <i>n</i> drawer. <i>Túa sa kumúda
sa ákung lamísa</i>, It's in the drawer in my
table.

<b>kumudkumud</b> <i>v</i> [A; b3c5] mumble under
one's breath in complaint. <i>Mukumudkumud
nà siyag sugúun</i>, She mumbles under her
breath when she is told to do s.t. <i>Gamay ra
nang trabahúang ikakumudkumud</i>, That
work is too light to grumble about. <b>kumudkumuran</b>
<i>a</i> tending to mumble under one's
breath.

<b>kumúhuy = KALAMÚHUY.</b>

<b>kumulga, kumulg[va]r</b> <i>v</i> [AN; b6] take Holy
Communion. <i>Adlaw-adlaw siya mukumulga</i>,
She takes Communion daily. <b>-nti</b> <i>n</i> one who
takes Holy Communion. <b>-siyun</b> <i>n</i> Holy
Communion.

<b>kumun</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> common, ordinary. <i>Kumun kaá</i>-*
-----File: 1041.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*yu nà dinhi. Daghan man gud</i>, That's awfully
common here. There is so many of them.
<b>2</b> ordinary, not special. <i>Kumun kaáyung
pagkáun</i>, Very ordinary food. <b>3</b> shared equally
among all the members of a group.
<i>Kining yutáa wà pa mabáhin. Kumun kini</i>,
This land hasn't been divided yet. It belongs
to everyone in the family. <i>Mísa karun nga
kumun álang sa tanang kalag sa purgaturyu</i>,
This is a common mass for all souls in purgatory.
<i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B126; a2] become common.
<i>Dílì madúgay makumun na sab ang tag-as
nga sanínà</i>, It won't be long before long
dresses get to be a common sight. <b>2</b> [c1]
make s.t. common property, shared by
many in a group. <i>Ug way tistamintu</i>, [**space inserted]<i>makumun</i>
<i>ang kabílin</i>, If there is no will, the inheritance
becomes common property. <b>sintídu</b>
-- <i>n</i> common sense.

<b>kúmun</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; a12] crumple s.t. up into a
ball, put s.t. that can be crumpled s.w. carelessly
without folding it or smoothing it
out. <i>Kumúna na lang nang mga sinínà sa
malíta</i>, Just throw those dresses into the
suitcase any old way. <i>Ayaw kumúna nang
papil kay magámit pa ang luyu</i>, Don't crumple
up those papers because we can still use
the back. <b>2</b> [A; a2] wrap s.t. up by just
crumpling the wrapper. <i>Kumúna lang ang
mga hirpin sa panyù</i>, Just wrap up the hair-*pins
in the handkerchief. <b>3</b> [A; a] hold s.t.
in the fist. <i>Kumúna pag-áyu ang kwarta arun
dì mahúlug</i>, Hold the money tightly in your
fist so it won't fall.

<b>kumunal</b> <i>n</i> for public use. <i>Ang kasilyas sa
mirkádu kumunal</i>, The comfort stations in
the market are for public use.

<b>kumungkumung = ALIKÚMÙ.</b>

<b>kumunikasiyun</b> <i>n</i> communication.

<b>kumunismu</b> <i>n</i> communism.

<b>kumunista</b> <i>n</i> communist. <i>a</i> ill-mannered,
grasping. <i>Kumunista ka giyud. Bísag gibahínan,
nangílug pa giyud</i>, What a grasping
sort you are. You have been given your
share, but you still want s.o. else's share!

<b>kumusta</b> how is (was, are, etc.). <i>Kumusta ka?</i>
How are you? <i>Kumusta ang ímung pagbisíta?</i>
How was your visit? <i>Kumusta ang ímung

How is your child? Has he finished

1 ask how s.o. is, send regards. <i>Aníay íyang
sulat nangumusta kanátung tanan</i>, Here's a
letter from him asking how we all are. <i>Ipangumusta
lang kung Pápa mu</i>, Give your

<b>kúmut</b> <i>v</i> [AN; ab2] <b>1</b> lay hands on any part
of the body including the hair and squeezing
or clawing at it. <i>Kumútun ku nang nawung
mu</i>, I'll claw your face. <b>2</b> crumple in
the hands. <i>Kumúta ang papil úsà ilábay</i>,
Crumple the paper before throwing it away.
<i>Kalamì rang kumútun sa bátà</i>, How I would
love to squeeze that chubby baby. <b>3</b> extract
the juice of s.t. by squeezing. <i>Akuy
mukúmut sa amirul nga bugas</i>, I'll get starch
for the laundry by squeezing the cooked
rice. <b>3a</b> [A; b] put salt on s.t. and squeeze
it to remove undesirable properties in the
juice. <i>Kumúti ug asin ang paliya arun makúhà
ang pait</i>, Squeeze the bitter vegetable
together with salt to remove its bitter taste.
<b>4</b> wash small pieces of clothing in a basin.
<i>Kumúti ang mga kamisin sa kabatáan</i>, Wash
out the children's undershirts. <b>5</b> [A2; a12]
afflict with anguish, grief, etc. <b>Ang mapait
níyang mga púlung mikúmut sa íyang kasingkásing</b>,
His bitter words clawed at her
heart.

<b>kum-ut = GUM-UT.</b>

<b>kun 1</b> if. <i>Kun mau kanà, iitsa ta ikaw sa kaláyu</i>,
If that is the case, I will toss you into
the fire. <i>Kun maarang, adtu na lang sa prusintu
pangatarúngan</i>, Please (lit. if it is all
right), explain at the precinct. <i>Ang ákung
ngálan si Husi Krus kun adúnay isúgù</i>, My
name is Joe Cruz. At your service (lit. if
you have anything to command). <i>Kun wà
pa nímu iúlì ang awtu, ikíha ta ka</i>, If you
hadn't returned the car, I would have filed a
case against you. <b>1a</b> when [so-and-so] happens.
<i>Kun mulakaw na siya pahibalua ku</i>,
When he goes, tell me. <i>Kun ting-init dinhi,
ínit giyud</i>, During the hot season it is really
hot. <b>1b</b> if, whether. <i>Pangutan-a si Máma mu
kun haúnun na ba ring kík</i>, Ask your Mother
if I should take the cake out of the oven. <b>2</b>
-----File: 1043.png--------------------------------------------------------
<b>-- dílì 2a</b> if not. <b>2b</b> except. <i>Way láin makasulbad
sa ákung suliran kun dílì ikaw</i>, No
one can solve my problem except you. <b>2c
dílì (walà) lang ... kun dì 2c1</b> not only ...
but also. <i>Wà lang gánì siya magmuru nákù,
kun dì milingiw pa giyud</i>, He not only
frowned at me but even turned his back

dríl dílì lámang káhuy ang gigámit kun
dílì ripli giyud</i>, In their drill they did not
use wooden guns but rather real rifles. <b>3</b>
<i>expression to introduce an explanatory
phrase:</i> that is to say. <i>Ang mga gradwádu
karun walay kadásig sa pagtuun kun sa pagtukì
sa kinaadman</i>, The recent graduates
have no enthusiasm for study that is to say,
to delve into knowledge.

<b>kunsinsiya</b> <i>n</i> conscience. <b>gastu ang, sa</b> -- <i>v</i>

<b>kunsint[vi]r</b> <i>v</i> [A2] allow s.o. who is in one's
charge to do s.t. wrong: either by helping
him overtly or by closing the eyes to it. <i>Ug
makasalà mi, dì giyud mukunsint[vi]r ákung

My mother won't go along with it if

<b>kunsirtu = KUNSIYIRTU.</b>

<b>kunsisiyun, kunsisyun</b> <i>n</i> concession, right
given to exploit natural resources, usually
forest or sea resources. <i>May kunsisiyun sila
sa kalasangan sa Mulábi</i>, They have a concession
in the forest of Molave. <i>v</i> [A1; a2]
get a certain concession. <i>Singkuwinta ka iktarya
ang íyang gikunsisyun álang sa íyang
pastu</i>, He obtained a concession of fifty hectares
for his ranch. <b>-aryu</b> <i>n</i> concessionaire.

<b>kunsiyirtu</b> <i>n</i> concert. <i>v</i> [A13; c] hold a concert.
<i>Nagkunsirtu na sad dinhi kay kastígu
hiniral</i>, We're having a concert (of crying)
again because everybody got punished. <i>Púru
mga klasika mauy ílang ikunsiyirtu</i>, They
will present a concert of purely classical
music.

legality. <b>2</b> in accordance with the constitu-*

Lim</i>, Those buildings were constructed

<b>kunsumisiyun</b> <i>n</i> intense grief that wastes
away the body. <i>Ikay ákung kunsumisiyun,
bataána ka</i>, You'll be the death of me. <i>Kunsumisiyun
ang gikamatyan sa asáwang gibiyáan</i>,
The wife wasted away and died of
grief after she was abandoned. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B16; a4][**joined a & 4]
be afflicted with grief that wastes away
the body. <i>Gikunsumisiyun (nagkunsumisiyun)
ang inahan sa kamaldítu sa anak</i>, The
mother wasted in grief because of her wayward
son. <b>2</b> [B1456; b3] worry very much
over a trifle. <i>Ngánung magkunsumisiyun ka
man ánang druwínga ug dì giyud mahímù?</i>
Why do you have to worry yourself to
death over that drawing if you can't do it?

<b>kunsumpsiyun = KUNSÚMU.</b>

<b>kunsúmu</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> consumption. <i>Dakug kunsúmu
ning awtúha</i>, This car uses a lot of gas. <i>Mínus
karun kitag kunsúmu sa túbig</i>, We use
less water now. <b>2</b> provisions, food supplies.
<i>Kun muadtu mu sa isla, pagdala ug kunsúmu
kay way pagkáun didtu</i>, If you go to
the island, bring provisions because there is
no food there. v [A] consume. <i>Mukunsúmu
mig tagsa ka bákid bugas bulanbúlan</i>, We
consume a cavan of rice each month.

<b>kunsurti</b> <i>n</i> consort of a reigning beauty
queen or muse. <i>v</i> [AB156; c1] become, be
the consort.

<b>kunsuylu</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> s.t. that makes s.t. unpleasant
easier to bear. <i>Bug-at ning trabahúa apan
kunsuylu sab ning magswildu tag sayu</i>, The
-----File: 1051.png--------------------------------------------------------
work is hard, but one thing that makes it
easier to bear is that we are paid early. <b>2</b>
improvement, a happy sign in s.t. that had
been distressing. <i>Sukad siya madapati sa
tambal, may kunsuylu na ang íyang pangláwas</i>,
Since she has been taking that medicine,
there has been an improvement in her
health. <b>3</b> situation that provokes enjoyment,
fun. <i>Wà tay kunsuylu áning tindahánang
magpalit kay púlus magmug-ut ang
mga tindíra</i>, We get no pleasure in buying
in that store because the salesgirls are all
unfriendly. <b>4</b> advantageous. <i>Kunsuylu ning
may awtu kay dílì lisud sa pagpaúlì</i>, It is an
advantage to have a car because it is no
problem to get home. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A123P; a] give
consolation, make s.t. easier to bear. <i>Bísag
sulat makakunsuylu na kaáyu sa kamíngaw
ku kanímu</i>, A letter from you would be
enough to console me in my loneliness for
you. <i>Pabakasyuna siya pára ikunsuylu sa
íyang kapakyásan sa burd</i>, Give him a vacation
to give him solace and comfort after
his frustration in the board exams. <b>2</b> [B; b6][**joined b & 6]
for a situation to provoke excitement,
delight. <i>Mukunsuylu ang dúwà ug payitpáyit
ang tím</i>, A game gets more fun if the
teams are equally good. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A; b] give
consolation. <i>n</i> s.t. which can give consolation.

<b>kuntadur</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> meter. <i>Ngánu gung dus písus
nga písus ra man ang náa sa kuntadur?</i> Why
two pesos, when the meter reads only one
peso? <b>-- sa túbig</b> water meter. <b>2</b> scorer,
scorekeeper. <i>v</i> [A1; ac1] have a meter.

<b>kuntak</b> <i>n</i> contact, connection in an organization
or high places. <i>Basta nigusyanti daghang
kuntak</i>, A businessman has to have
lots of contacts. <i>v</i> [A; a] contact, get in
touch with. <i>Kun makigkuntak ka níya, tawga
lang sa tilipunu</i>, If you want to get in
contact with her, just call her on the telephone.
<i>Inig-abut sa mayur, kuntáka dáyun
ku</i>, As soon as the mayor arrives, contact
me immediately.

<b>kunt[va]r</b> <i>v</i> [A; c1] <b>1</b> keep score, count a
score. <i>Tulu ka táwu ang mukunt[va]r (magkunt[va]r)
sa buksing: ang ripiri ug ang duha
ka huwis</i>, In a boxing three persons keep
the score: the referee and the two judges.
<i>Dílì tu níya kuntarun (ikunt[va]r) kay páwul
man</i>, He won't count that shot because
they had called a foul. <i>Ikunt[va]r (kuntara) sa
papil ang matag puntus níla</i>, Mark a score
for each point they make on a piece of paper.
<b>2</b> shout out the score. <i>Ikunt[va]r (kuntara)
ang matag puntus</i>, Shout out the score
every time s.o. makes a point.

<b>kuntidyus</b> <i>n</i> contagious ward in a hospital.

<b>kuntimpuraryu</b> <i>n</i> contemporary, one living
in the same era as another or being in a certain
association at the same time. <i>Kuntimpuraryu
si Aginaldu ni Risal</i>, Aguinaldo
was a contemporary of Rizal's.[**should be "Rizal"] <i>Kuntimpuraryu

<b>kuntininti</b> <i>n</i> continent.

<b>kuntintu</b> <i>a</i> satisfied, contented. <i>Dì ku kuntintu
sa ákung swildu</i>, I'm not satisfied with
my salary. <i>v</i> [B12; b6] be, become satisfied.
Wà ku makuntintu adtung kaúna, I
wasn't satisfied with that meal. <b>kakuntintuhun</b>
<i>n</i> state of reaching contentment. <i>Dúnay
mga babáyi nga way kakuntintuhun</i>,
There are women that are impossible to
satisfy (sexually).

<b>kuntis</b> <i>n</i> a contest, competition. <i>Kuntis sa
áwit</i>, Singing contest. <i>v</i> [AC; ab] have a
contest. <i>Kuntísun nátù kun kinsa giyuy maáyung
láki</i>, We must have a contest to determine
who is really the best. <i>Ispíling ang
ílang gikuntísan</i>, They will have a spelling
bee.

<b>kuntra</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> s.t. contrary to one's liking. <i>Kuntra
ku giyud nang táwung palahúbug</i>, I very
much dislike people who drink too much.
<b>1a -- sa dugù</b> s.t. that is regarded with aversion.
<i>Kuntra sa ákung dugù ang mga maut</i>,
I loathe people who are hypocrites. <b>1b --
gustu</b> done against one's will. <i>Kuntra gustu
siyang mitúman</i>, She complied against her
will. <b>1c -- hitsu</b> for a body or s.t. manufactured
to be unproportional in build or structure.
<i>Kuntra hitsu kaáyu siya kay tambuk
unyà gagmayg bitíis</i>, She is out of proportion
because she is fat but her legs are small.
<b>1d -- kumpas</b> out of time, not in rhythm.
<b>1e1 -- partídu</b> political opponent. <i>Magsúun
nga kuntra partídu sa pulitika apan dílì sa
lamísa</i>, Brothers and sisters may be opponents
in politics but not in their relationships
with each other. <b>1e2</b> people who are
always opposed to everything. <i>Mga kuntra
partídu kaáyu nang mga tawhána sa tanan
tang buhátun, dì maáyung iuban sa punduk</i>,
Those people are always opposed to everything
we do. Let's not include them in our
group. <i>v</i> [B23(1)6C] be, become political
opponents or always oppose s.o. else's
views or stand. <b>1f -- tyimpu</b> an impediment
to a course of action to be done in the future.
<i>Ug way kuntra tyimpu, karung Duminggu
mag-ayskrim ta</i>, If nothing gets in
-----File: 1053.png--------------------------------------------------------
the way, we can have ice cream on Sunday.
<b>2a</b> causing unpleasant bodily reaction to
s.o. <i>Kuntra sa húbak ang pasáyan</i>, Shrimps
are bad for asthma. <b>2b</b> remedy for s.t. bad.
<i>Kuntra sa húbak kining tablítas</i>, These tablets
are good for asthma. <b>2b1 -- sa ampay</b>
love s.t. very much (humorous--lit. it's a
remedy for my craving). <i>Mukáun ug inasal?
Kuntra nà sa ákung ampay!</i> Do I like roast
pig? No, I love it! <b>3 -- sa</b> opposed to, rather
than. <i>Maáyu na lang ning makalilímus
kuntra nímu nga kawatan</i>, It's better to be
a beggar than to be like you, a thief. <i>Mas
maáyu ang bínu kuntra sa túbà</i>, Wine is
much better than palm toddy. <i>Maíbug kahà
ku níya kuntra nímu?</i> Would I be attracted
to him more than to you? <b>4 -- ug</b> [such-and-such]
an amount bet against [so-and-so]
much. <i>Ímung pusta singku kuntrag
kwatru</i>, I bet him five to four. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> enemy
or opponent. <i>Kuntra sa Inglatíra ang Alimanya</i>,
Germany was Britain's enemy. <i>Kuntra
si Ilurdi ni Usáka</i>, Osaka was Elorde's
opponent. <b>2</b> in folk belief, s.t. used to drive
away evil spirits, usually hidden in one's
clothing. <b>3</b> s.t. used to reinforce s.t. which
is placed at the other side of it. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AC; ab2][**joined ab & 2]
be, become hostile to each other. <i>Dì ku
mukuntra ug parinti</i>, I won't act hostilely
toward my relatives. <i>Nagkakuntra ang managsúun
tungud sa kabílin</i>, The brothers became
enemies on account of the inheritance.
<i>Nakuntrahan (gikuntra) ang íyang trátu sa
ginikánan</i>, Her parents took a dislike to her
suitor. <b>2</b> [A2C; ac3] oppose s.o. in a contest,
politics, and the like. <i>Dílì siya mukuntra
ug dakù níya</i>, He won't play against anyone
bigger than he is. <i>Kuntráhun nímu sila
sa pagkamayur nga paryinti man?</i> Are you
going to oppose them in the mayoralty contest
when they are your relatives? <i>Ikaw
mauy ikuntra námù níya</i>, We will pit you
against him. <b>3</b> [c6] use as a remedy. <i>Kining
tablítas ikakuntra sa tulug</i>, These tablets
are good to take to keep you awake. <b>4</b> [c]
be [so-and-so] much against [such-and-such]
an amount. <i>Sigurádu man kahà ka,
kuntráhan ta nang diyis mug singku</i>, If
you're so sure, I'll bet five pesos against
your ten. <b>5</b> [A12] wear s.t. sewn in the
clothing to drive away evil spirits. <b>6</b> [c]
put a reinforcement behind s.t. <i>Kuntráhi
(kuntrahi) nang gitaúras batúnis arun dílì
magísì</i>, Put a reinforcement behind where
you sew on the botton[**button] so it won't rip. <b>6a =
BALINSIYÁNA</b>, <i>v</i> <b>2. -in-</b> <i>n</i> a seam sewn with
the <i>balinsiyána</i> stitch. <b>paN-</b> <i>n</i> s.t. worn as
protection against s.t.[+]

<b>kuntrabandu</b> <i>n</i> contraband. <i>v</i> [B1256] be

ang butang nga dílì ipaági sa ku</i>stum,
Smuggled goods that don't pass the Customs

<i>n</i> smuggler, one who deals in contraband

<b>kuntrabída</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> a villain in a drama or story.
<b>2</b> one who acts like a villain, spoiling or opposing

Máma uy, dì ku patambúngun sa parti</i>,
Mother is a killjoy, she won't let me attend

<b>kuntra gustu</b> <i>see</i> <b>GUSTU.</b>

<b>kuntraktur</b> <i>n</i> contractor for the construction

<i>Pruyiktu sa gubiyirnu nga ákung gikuntraktúran</i>,
Government projects for which I
was the contractor.

<b>kuntraryu</b> <i>a</i> being enemies. <i>Kuntraryu mi kaáyu
kay wà siyay batásan</i>, We're enemies
because he has no manners. <i>v</i> [C1] be enemies
with each other.

<b>kuntrasinyas</b> <i>n</i> password or secret signal. <i>Ug
muhíngus ku, kuntrasinyas nà nga wíting ku</i>,
If I sniffle, it's a sign that I'm about to go
rummy. <i>Unsay kuntrasinyas sa pagsúd sa
kampu?</i> What is the password to enter the
camp? <i>Dúnay kuntrasinyas ang balúta arun
hibaw-an nga mibutar ka nákù</i>, There's a
secret mark on the ballot so we know you
voted for me. <i>v</i> [A3; c6] give a word or secret
signal.

<b>kuntráta, kuntrátu</b> <i>n</i> written contract or verbal
agreement. <i>Pilay kuntrátu sa matadíru
íning ímung bábuy?</i> What price have you
agreed upon with the butcher for your pig?
<i>v</i> [ANC2; c] make a contract or verbal bargain.
<i>Nagkuntrátu kug sakyanan pára sa átung
ikskursiyun</i>, I have already made an
agreement for our transportation on the excursion.
<b>kuntratádu</b> <i>a</i> bound with a contract
or oral agreement. <i>Kuntratádu na ning
babúya</i>, This pig has already been spoken
for. <b>kuntratista</b> <i>n</i> one who buys and sells
things or services on a professional basis,
contracting for the things bought or services
rendered. <i>Kuntratista sa bábuy</i>, One
who buys and sells pigs. <i>Kuntratista sa hákut</i>,
One who contracts to haul things. <i>v</i>
[B156] be, become a contractor of this
sort.

<b>kuntribusiyun</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> financial contribution. <b>2</b>
tax on real property. <i>v</i> [A1; c] give a contribution
or pay a real property tax.

<b>kuntringkanti</b> <i>n</i> opponents in a political election.
<i>v</i> [C; ac3] be opponents for electoral
-----File: 1055.png--------------------------------------------------------
office. <i>Dì sila maáyung kuntringkantíhun
kay manag-ágaw sila</i>, They should not be
made to oppose each other because they
are cousins. <i>Bag-ángang pulitiku ang ákung
gikakuntringkanti</i>, The man I fought against
was a seasoned politician.

<b>*kuntrisiyun aktu sa --</b> <i>n</i> Act of Contrition.

<b>kuntr[vu]l</b> <i>n</i> control over s.o.'s actions, discipline.
<i>Ang mayur way kuntr[vu]l sa kapulisan</i>,
The mayor has no control over his police
force. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A] control oneself or the actions
of s.t. else. <i>Nagkuntr[vu]l lang giyud ku
nga dì makapangísug</i>, I did my best to control
my temper. <i>Wà na ku makakuntr[vu]l sa
manubíla</i>, I couldn't control the wheel
any longer. <b>2</b> [C2] exercise birth control.
<i>Wà mi magkuntr[vu]l, maung daghan mig anak</i>,
We didn't practice birth control so we
had lots of children.

<b>kuntrular</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] control s.t. <i>Kuntrulaha
ang inyung mga bátà</i>, Control your children.
<i>Gikuntrular sa mga Huk ang Sintral
Lusun</i>, The Huks control Central Luzon.
<i>Ang pamaligyag bugas gikuntrular sa mga
Insik</i>, The rice trade is controlled by the
Chinese. <b>kuntruládu, kuntruláwu</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> in the
control of. <i>Ang Kunggrísu kuntruládu sa
Nasyunalista</i>, The Congress is in the control
of the Nacionalista Party. <b>2</b> under control,
subdued. <i>Kuntruládu na ang mga prísu nga
nagráyut</i>, The prisoners that rioted are now
under control. <i>3</i> done with control. <i>Kuntruládu
ang íyang paghapak sa búla maung
nasúd ni sa lungag</i>, He drives the golf ball
with control. That's why it goes into the
hole.

<b>kuntud_{1}</b> <i>v</i> [AB; b2c1] decrease in amount
or quantity. <i>Mukuntud (makuntud) ang tubà
sa tinghangin</i>, The coconut palm toddy
yields less when it is windy. <i>Dì siya makakuntud
sa íyang pagkáun</i>, She can't cut
down on her food intake.

<b>kuntud_{2}</b> a for the surface of a piece of land
to be uneven. <i>Ayúha pagpátag kay kuntud
pa kanang dapíta dihà</i>, Level that part carefully.
It is still bulging there. <i>v</i> [B; c12] be,
become uneven. <i>Ipapátag sa buldúsir kanang
dápit nga nagkuntud</i>, Have the bulldozer
level that part where it is bulging.

<b>kuntúdu</b> <i>a</i> elaborate, having all the trimmings.
<i>Kuntúdu siyang mamisti</i>, She is

<b>kunu</b> <i>short form</i>: <b>nu</b> <b>1</b> it is @said, s.o. said.
<i>Namatay kunu ag pilútu</i>, They say the pilot

that he is not under obligation to obey it--i.e.,

on the chance that. <i>Madúgay pa ba

magkurpurasiyun lang ta kay singkwinta
rang ákù diri</i>, Let's have a drinking spree,
-----File: 1070.png--------------------------------------------------------
but let us pool our money because I only

<b>kurta_{2}</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> for eggs or milk to be spoiled, usually

<b>kurti_{1}</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> measure of cloth cut in advance.

<i>Wà pa gániy nakakurti, íya nang gipanghátag
ang mga baráha</i>, No one has cut the

ag míd, mikurti sab ku</i>, While they

into their conversation. <b>3a</b> participate in the

mats quickly. <i>v</i> [B3; c1] do s.t. rapidly.
<i>Makútù (mukútù) ang dágan ánang rilúha
ug yawíhan</i>, That watch runs fast when you
wind it. <i>Ug ímung kutúun (ikútù) pagsulti,
dì ku makasabut nímu</i>, When you talk rapidly,
I can't make out anything you say.

<b>kútù_{2}</b> <i>n</i> @creak or @{cracking sound}. <i>v</i> [A2; a12][**joined a & 12]
creaking or cracking noise. <i>Mikútù ang
salug nga kawáyan sa ákung pagtunub</i>, The

branch made a cracking sound and then
broke. <b>kutùkutù</b> <i>v</i> [A] make a crackling
noise. <i>Mukutùkutù ang sitsarun inig-úsap</i>,
Fried pork rinds make a crackling noise
when you chew them.

<b>kutub</b> <i>a</i> having wrinkles sewn into it. <i>v</i> [B6]
for sewing to come out so that wrinkles
appear in unintended places. <i>Mukutub (makutub)
ang buktun sa ímung sinínà ug dì
nímu ilagdà</i>, The sleeves of your dress will
come out wrinkled if you sew them directly
without basting them.

<b>kútub</b> <b>1</b> @{as far as} a certain point in space or
time. <i>Kútub ang karsáda sa Bukánu</i>, The
road reaches as far as Bocano. <i>Kining trabahúa
kútub ra sa Disimbri</i>, This job will
last only to December. <i>Ása kútub kining
dalána?</i> Where does this road go up to? <b>1a</b>
<b>-- sa</b> [<i>word referring to action</i>] only as
much as doing, no more than. <i>Kútub ra sa
paghisgut, way líhuk</i>, They only went so
far as to discuss it. They didn't take any action.
<b>2</b> @{as much as}. <i>Gikúhà níla kútub sa
ílang madala</i>, They took as much as they
could carry. <b>2a</b> @whatever, @anyone. <i>Patákà
ka lag tubag kútub sa ímung mahunàhunaan</i>,
You just take a stab saying whatever
enters your head. <b>3</b> <b>-- karun</b> starting @now.
<i>Kútub karun dì na ka mamisíta nákù</i>, From
now on don't visit me any more. <b>-in-an</b>,
<b>kinutbánan</b> <i>n</i> @end, @limit. <i>Walay kinutúban
ning ákung pag-antus</i>, My suffering has no
-----File: 1091.png--------------------------------------------------------

<i>Ug mukútub sa alas utsu ang prugráma,
makapanini pa ka</i>, If the program doesn't
last later than eight o'clock, you still have

embers. <i>Nagkiyungkung [**note: spelling variant not flagged] pa gihápun ka
dihà bísag taas na ang adlaw?</i> You are still
curled up there, even at this hour of the day?

<b>kyusku</b> <i>n</i> a @kiosk in a park or plaza, usually
used as a bandstand or a place for resting.
<i>v</i> [b6] put a kiosk up s.w.

<b>kyuskus</b> = <sc>KUYUSKUS</sc>.

<b>kyúum</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B; c1] for s.t. with a horizontal
opening to @close tightly. <i>Mukyúum ang imbaw
ug matugaw</i>, Clams shut tight when
they are disturbed. <i>Makyúum nang samára</i>,
That wound will close. <i>Nagkakyúum ang
mga dáhun sa akasya nga nagkagabíi na</i>, The
acacia leaves are slowly closing up as night
is drawing near. <b>2</b> keep the mouth shut and
-----File: 1104.png--------------------------------------------------------
not talk. <i>Mukyúum nà siya ug hisagpaan</i>,
She'll shut up if you slap her. <i>Kyuúmun
(ikyúum) ku lang ang tinúud nga nahitabù</i>,
I'll just keep my mouth shut as to what
really happened. <b>3</b> [B; a1P] be doubled
-----File: 1105.png--------------------------------------------------------
up in fear or pain. <i>Mikyúum siya sa pagkaigù
níya sa kutukutu</i>, He doubled up
from pain when he was hit in the solar

<b>la_{1}</b> = <sc>LÁMANG</sc> (dialectal).

<b>la_{2}</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @la, the sixth note in the musical scale.

when singing a song.

<b>láag</b> <i>v</i> [A; ac] @roam about for no special purpose,
just for diversion. <i>Atúa si Pidru sa
syudad miláag</i>, Pedro is downtown roaming
about. <i>Unsay ímung laágun didtu? Mangítà
na pud kag áway?</i> What are you going
to roam around there for? Are you looking
for another fight? <b>(->)</b> <i>a</i> roving about, going
nowhere in particular. <i>Lagmit paangkan
ang babáying laag</i>, A woman that roams
about is likely to get pregnant. <i>Ang laag
<i>n</i>íyang panan-aw didtu mahiúrung sa babáyi</i>,
His roving gaze stopped at the woman.
<i>v</i> [B12] get to be a wanderer. <b>-an(->)</b> =
<sc>LAAG</sc>.

<b>láang</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @noose of a trap. <i>Biraha ang láang
inigtunub sa manuk</i>, Pull the noose when
the chicken steps in. <i>1a</i> any trap that has a
noose. <b>2</b> stratagem designed to catch or
trick s.o. <i>Babáyi ang gamíta nga láang pagsíkup
sa ispíya</i>, Use a woman as a trap to
snare the spy. <i>v</i> [A; a] <b>1</b> trap s.t. with a
noose. <i>Laángun <i>n</i>átung bábuy</i>, Let's trap
the pig with a noose. <b>2</b> employ a trick to
catch s.o. <i>Dì siya madiritsu ug dakup. Laángun
giyud</i>, He can't be caught easily. He
should be trapped. <b>-in-</b> = <sc>LÁANG</sc>, <i>n1</i>.

<b>laas</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; c] take a sword or rod and raise
it. <i>Naglaas ug sundang ang hurimintádu</i>,
The amok was brandishing a bolo. <i>Gilaas
sa tigúlang ang íyang ulísi</i>, The old man
raised his cane in the air. <b>2</b> [A13; b6] go
bare of protection. <i>Naglaas ka lang nga tugnaw
kaáyu?</i> Why aren't you dressed when
it's so cold?

<b>láas</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] <b>1</b> @tear leaves or thin sheets
lengthwise into strips. <i>Miláas siyag papil pára
himúung bandirabandíra</i>, She tore some
papers into strips to make into pennants. <b>2</b>
-----File: 1107.png--------------------------------------------------------
@tear, @peel s.t. off from an attachment. <i>Nakaláas
ku sa bulsa sa íyang púlu</i>, I accidentally
tore the pocket off his shirt. <i>Ang uban nga

people just peel the skin off of goats. <b>2a</b> remove
the cloth-like sheathing of the coconut
bud as the first step in tapping the toddy.
<i>n</i> <b>1</b> the lower part of the leaves of the

Several pieces of dry palm frond sheaths of

cloth-like sheath of the coconut bud which

<b>laaw</b> <i>n</i> @{stray cat}.

<b>láay</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @monotonous, wearingly boring. <i>Láay
kaáyu ning wà tay búhat</i>, It is so dull to
be without anything to do. <i>Láay kaáyu ang
pagpaábut</i>, It is very boring just to wait around.
<b>2</b> disgusting, disappointing in that
one doesn't conform to what is expected of
him. <i>Laáya nímu uy, ingun ka palitan ku
nímug sapátus</i>, How disgusting! You promised
to buy shoes for me (but you didn't).
<i>Kaláay bayang Nína, gipanabì diay níya ang
ákung sikrítu</i>, How disgusting of Nina. She
told my secret to everybody. <i>v</i> [B124; b4]
be boring, feel bored. <i>Nagkalaay na ning
trabahúa kay mu ra gihápun</i>, This work is
getting boring because it is always the same
thing. <i>Mipaúlì na lang siya kay gilaáyan nag
pinaábut nímu</i>, He just went home. He got
tired of waiting for you. <b>(->)</b> <i>n</i> a variety of
corn that takes a long time to mature. <b>laaylaay</b>
<i>v</i> [A; b(1)] while away time or do s.t.
for the meantime. <i>Samtang magpaábut ku
mulaaylaay lang kug gansilyu</i>, While I'm
waiting, I'll while away the time crocheting.
<i>Gilaaylaayan ku lang nig búhat, nahuman
na giyud</i>, I just did this little by little during
-----File: 1108.png--------------------------------------------------------
my spare time, and now it's finished. <b>ka-(->)</b>
= <sc>LAAYLAAY</sc>. <b>ka-</b> <i>n</i> boredom.

<b>láb_{1}</b> <i>n</i> half of the number of points or one
less half the number of points that make a
tennis or pingpong game. (From the notion
that when the one who is behind reaches
half the number of points--usually ten
points, that number is subtracted from the
winner's points and the one behind is reckoned
at zero. E.g. a score 12 to 10 is reckoned
at <i>dus láb</i> instead of <i>dúsi diyis</i>.) <i>v</i> [A; b6]
for the one who is behind to get as far
as the half-way point. <i>Makaláb lang ku, sigurádu
giyud kung makaagpas ug makadaug</i>,
If I can make it to love (ten points), I'm
sure I can catch up and win. <i>Siya ang kampiyun
apan gilában ku siya</i>, He is the champion,
but I was able to get ten points (out
of twenty-one).

<b>láb_{2}</b> <i>n</i> lab.

<b>laba</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; b1] @{wash clothing}. <i>Gilabhan níya

pace. labhanan <i>n</i> <b>1</b> dirty laundry. <b>2</b> place
to do wash. <b>3</b> place to air grievances. <i>labhunun</i>
= <sc>LABHANAN</sc>, <i>n1</i>. <b>nilabhan</b> (<b>linabhan</b>)

<b>lab-ak</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AB; a] get to have spaces or omissions

<b>labanus</b> <i>n</i> @radishes. The white (Chinese) radishes
are the variety most commonly grown
in Cebu.

<b>labas_{1}</b> (from <i>lab-as</i>) <i>v</i> [AN; a2c] @vend or @peddle
fish that one has bought (usually from
the fisherman). <i>Naglabas lang ang íyang anak
únà kay wà pa makasulud ug trabáhu</i>,
Her daughter works buying and selling fish
for the while because she doesn't have a job.
<i>Ilabas ring ákung kuhà</i>, Peddle my catch.
<b>-íra</b> female fish vendor. <b>-íru</b> = <sc>LABASÍRA</sc>
(male).

<b>labas_{2}</b> = <sc>GULÀ</sc> (used only by speakers
strongly influenced by Tagalog). <b>pa-</b> <i>n</i> boast,
ostentatious display. <i>Ayaw tug tuúhi ang
íyang hílak, palabas lang tu</i>, Don't pay attention
to his crying fit. That was just a
put-on.

<b>labas_{3}</b> <i>v</i> [A; ab7] spend entrusted money
for oneself. <i>Gilabasan kug diyútay ang ímung
gibílin nákù</i>, I used some of the money
you had me keep for you.

<b>lab-as</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> for s.t. quickly perishable to be
@fresh. <i>Lab-as nga hángin</i>, @Fresh air. <i>Lab-as
nga balità</i>, Fresh news. <i>Lab-as nga búlak</i>,
Fresh flowers. <i>Lab-as isdà</i>, @{Fresh fish}. <b>2</b>
fresh in manner. <i>Lab-as ra kaáyu nang ímung
panlihuklihuk</i>, Your actions are very
fresh. <i>n</i> fresh fish. <i>Musúruy siyag lab-as káda
buntag</i>, She peddles fresh fish every
morning. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B2] be fresh. <b>2</b> [AB2; a12]
make s.t. fresh to one's mind. <i>Mga handumánan
nga naglab-as sa átung kagahápun</i>,
Memories that keep our past fresh. <b>nilab-as</b>
<i>a</i> in a fresh way. <i>v</i> [a1] do s.t. in a fresh
way. <i>Ginilab-as ku <i>n</i>íyag pangutána</i>, He

<b>labaw</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B3; c] @{jut out higher than s.t.},

<b>lagi</b> particle used to assert emphatically that
s.t. is what it is. <b>1</b> <i>particle giving assurance
about s.t. the interlocutor may be inclined
to disbelieve:</i> believe it or not, I assure you
[so-and-so] is the case. <i>Ayaw ug kabaláka
kay muabut lagi si Máma mu,</i> Don't worry.
Your mother will come back. <i>Wà lagi nákù
tuyúa. Ayaw kasukù,</i> I told you I didn't
mean to do it. You shouldn't get angry. <b>1a</b>
<i>in narration, a particle acknowledging that
there might be reason to disbelieve:</i> believe
it or not. <i>Ang manuk lagi ni Pidru nga bayat
nakabunù,</i> Believe it or not, that weakling
cock of Pedro's managed to win! <b>1b</b>
<b>kay --</b> [**correction: -- kay] because, after all, that is what one
would expect. <i>Tungud lagi kay abtik man
tu siya, siyay nakadaug,</i> And since he was,
after all, pretty smart, he won. <b>2</b> expressing
surprise at s.t. contrary to one's expectations.
<i>Ingun kang wâ[**  !?]. Nía ra man lagi,</i> You
said it was gone, but here it is! <i>Ingun kang
dílì mulubad, milubad man lagi,</i> You said it
wasn't going to fade, but it did. <b>2a</b> <b>náa na
pud --</b> expression of deep exasperation at
s.t. that occured [**typo for occurred] a second time, which already
was exasperating to start out with.
<i>Náa na pud lagi. Ímu na pung gihilabtan,</i>
There you go again. You touched it again.
<b>2b</b> <b>apan --</b> but despite what might have
been expected. <i>Apan lagi, dinhi puy pipila
nga nanambung,</i> However, there were a few
who attended. <b>2c</b> [so-and-so] is the case,
after all, much as one might wish it otherwise.
<i>Nalípay nga naadtu sa Amirika ang ílang
anak, piru kay anak man lagi, mingawun
giyud sila,</i> They are happy that their
son went to the States, but because he is,
after all, their son, they will miss him. <b>2d</b>
<i>with a repeated command or request:</i> didn't
I tell you to do [so-and-so]? Now do it!
<i>Ibutang lagi nang kutsilyu,</i> Didn't I tell you
to put that knife down? <i>Ayaw lagig sábà,</i> I
said stop that noise. <i>Tris lagi. Dì lagi ni ikatúgut
ug dus,</i> I said three. I told you I can't
let you have it for two. <b>3</b> <i>indicating that
the speaker was right all along about a certain
point in contention:</i> see, I told you.
<i>Lagi, giingnan ta lagi kang hustu tu,</i> See, I
-----File: 1132.png--------------------------------------------------------
told you that was right! <i>'Uu. Mubálik giyud
ku. Duul ra man.' -- 'Lagi,'</i> 'Yes, I will
come back again. Anyway, it's right close.'
-- 'Yes (that's what I've been saying).' <b>dáan
pa --</b> [<i>gen</i>.] that's what [gen.] thought. <i>Dáan
pa lagi ku, wà siya dinhi</i>, That's just what
I thought! He's not here. <b>3a</b> @conceding a
point with some reservation. <i>'Gwápu siyag
kutsi.' -- 'U lagi, piru inútang,'</i> 'He's got a
nice car.' -- 'He sure does, but it's not his.'
<i>v</i> [b(1)] emphatically assure s.o. by saying
<i>lagi</i> to him. <i>Dì ku musálig sa íyang pasálig
bísan ug gilagihan ku níya</i>, I won't count on
his promises even though he assured me
emphatically.

<b>lag-i</b> <i>n</i> thin piece of bamboo or rattan used

bamboo or rattan.

<b>lag-id_{2}</b> <i>v</i> [A; bc] @brush, @whizz, @{speed by} s.t.

grazed his face.

<b>lagilági</b> @kinds, @quality. <i>Lagilági ang buluk sa

to be a boy! <b>laláki</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> human male. <i>Laláki

man. <b>2</b> paramour. <i>Pusilun ku ang laláki sa
ákung asáwa,</i> I'll kill my wife's paramour.
<b>3</b> <b>-ng búhat</b> acting in a way proper to a man.
<i>Mu nay láking búhat nga makig-áwayg babáyi?</i>
Is that what a gentleman does--quarrel
with a woman? <b>4</b> <b>mau nay --</b> Atta boy,
that's the way you ought to do it (said only
to males). <b>la-(<-), panla-, panla-(<-)</b> <i>v</i> [A; a]
have a paramour. <i>Nanglaláki (naglalaki) ang
íyang asáwa,</i> His wife has a paramour. <i>Gipanglalaki
(gilalaki) níya ang íyang humagbus,</i>
She took her stepson for a lover. <b>-in-(<-)</b>
<i>a</i> done like a male; man-like. <i>Lináki ang
íyang tupi,</i> She has a man's haircut. <i>v</i> [A;
-----File: 1153.png--------------------------------------------------------
a] do things like a male. <i>Mulináki ku ug ímu

arun dì ka hiilhan nga báyut,</i> Carry yourself
like a man so people won't recognize that
you're a fairy. <b>-in-</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> man's bicycle. <b>2</b> riding

<b>*láki_{2} maáyung --</b> have exceptional ability.
<i>Maáyung láki si Maríya sa ininglis,</i> Maria has

<b>walay --</b> no good. <i>Way kaláki ang pagkáun

<i>Maprísu ta ánang kalakíha nímu,</i> We might
land in jail with those plans of yours. <b>3</b> doings,
usually evil. <i>Unsa tung inyung kaláki
sa Manílà?</i> What was going on in Manila?
<b>3a</b> way one does things. <i>Kanúnay kang malít
ug mau nang kalakíha,</i> You'll never be
on time if that's the way you do things. <b>3b</b>
<b>unsay ka-</b> how are things? <i>Unsay kaláki run
bay?</i> How are things, pal? <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [ANP; a1]

<i>Akuy mukaláki (mupakaláki, mangaláki) niíni
arun dílì magkúlang,</i> I'll do s.t. so that
this will be enough for all of us. <i>Kalakíha ri
ug mahímù pa ba ning pawuntin ping daut,</i>
See if you can do s.t. with this broken fountain
pen to make it work. <b>2</b> [A1P] do s.t.
one shouldn't be doing. <i>Nagkaláki (nagpakaláki)
ka dihag languylánguy ug malumus
ka,</i> You dare to swim where you shouldn't
be. You might drown. <i>Kaláki (pakaláki) kag
mulumakinilya ug sakpan ka sa tag-íya,</i> Better
stop playing with that typewriter. The

<sc>KALÁKI</sc>, <i>v.</i> <b>3</b> do one's best. <i>Magpakaláki

studies. <b>kalakíhan</b> <i>a</i> having an extraordinary

<b>lakip</b> including, included. <i>Lakip na niíning

ku mulakip ug kasábà sa way lábut,</i> I won't

<i>Nalakip tingáli ang risíbu sa sulat pagpadala,</i>
I must have accidentally enclosed the receipt
in the letter when I sent it.

sigh. <b>4</b> profound, hard to understand. <i>Lalum
nga tirminu,</i> Difficult terms. <i>Lalum

for a relapse after childbirth to be severe. <i>v</i>
<b>1</b> [AB; ab] deepen, cause to become deep.
<i>Ang kaminíru mauy mulalum sa mga kanal,</i>
The street cleaners will deepen the ditches.
<i>Mulalum (malalum) ang samad ug dílì limpiyúhan,</i>
A wound will become deep if it is
not cleaned. <i>Laluma pagbúhù ang lubung,</i>
Dig the grave deep enough. <i>Lalumi pag diyútay

<b>3</b> [B2] become deep and low, reaching
from the depths. <i>Milalum ang íyang pangaghu
nga nagtan-aw sa masakitun,</i> Her
sighs grew deeper as she looked at the sick
man. <b>4</b> [B2; b6] get to be profound. <i>Makalalum
(makapalalum) diay ug pinsamintu
ning kalisud,</i> I have found out that hardship
makes one think deeply. <b>5</b> <b>-- ang bughat</b>

<i>Ang kasagunsun sa pagpanganak mauy

<b>-g-</b> = <sc>LALUM</sc>, <i>a</i>, <i>v</i> (plural). <b>gi-un, giladmun</b>
<i>n</i> depth. <i>Ang giladmun sa íyang pangútuk,</i>
The depth of his intelligence. <b>ha-</b> <i>a</i> deep.

the fish net. <i>Pailadmi sa libru ang mga papil,</i>

It's difficult to get the book because

<b>lálung</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] <b>1</b> grow seedlings. <i>Maglálung

<b>lámang</b> <i>short form</i>: <b>lang.</b> @only, @just. <b>1</b> merely,
[do] nothing more than. <i>Naglingkud lang
siya didtu ug walà magtingug,</i> He just sat
-----File: 1161.png--------------------------------------------------------
there without saying anything. <i>Mutsátsu
lang siya unyà magbuut,</i> He's just a houseboy,
but he wants to have the say. <i>Walà ku
muanhi arun lang kasab-an,</i> I didn't come
here merely to get a scolding. <i>Ígù lang siya
sa paghílak,</i> All she could do was cry. (Lit.
She was merely up to crying.) <i>Káwang lang
ang ákung pag-antus,</i> My sufferings were all
in vain (nothing more than vain). <i>Barátu ni
kay písus lang,</i> This is cheap because it is
only a peso. <i>Tú lang ákung gidá,</i> I only
brought three. <b>1a</b> <i>with commands or exhortation:</i>
just do [so-and-so]--it's a small
thing to do. <i>Hulata lang ku sa gawas,</i> Just
wait for me outside. <i>Maglakaw lang ta, duul
ra man,</i> Let's just walk. It's not far. <b>1b</b> <b>sígi
--</b> please [do], it's just a little favor to ask.
<i>Sígi lang. Tugti lang ku,</i> Come on. Please,
let me do it. <b>1c</b> <i>with negatives:</i> not bother
to do. <i>Dì lang ta mangatúlug rung gabíi,</i>
Let's not bother going to sleep this evening.
<b>1c1</b> <b>walà (dílì) -- ... kun dílì ...</b> not only
... but also ... <i>Dì lang ang inahan kun dì
hasta anak maapiktahan,</i> Not only the
mother but also the child will be affected.
<b>1d</b> <b>basta --</b> just so it happens, though it
isn't desirable. <i>Iwarì lang nà. Basta lang mawálà
sa ákung panan-aw,</i> Get rid of it. Just
so it gets out of my sight. <b>1e</b> <b>karun, bag-u,
gahápun --</b> just now, just recently, just yesterday.
<i>Karun lang siya miabut,</i> He just arrived
now. <i>Bag-u lang silang namalhin,</i> They
just recently moved. <i>Gahápun lang siya maulì,</i>
He just went home yesterday. <b>1f</b> [<i>expression
of time</i>] -- just do at [such-and-such
time] (and no other time). <i>Mahuybis
lang sila mamasúra,</i> They just collect garbage
on Thursdays. <b>1g</b> <b>balu, ambut --</b> gee, I
don't know (I'm only up to saying I don't
know). <b>1h</b> <b>dipindi, sigun --, sa</b> [<i>verb</i>] -- depending
on. <i>Ákung ibaligyà sa makauna
lang,</i> I'll sell it to whoever is first. <i>Sigun
lang sa prisyu,</i> It depends on the price. <b>1i</b>
<b>gáni, gáling --</b> the only thing wrong. <i>Maáyu
untà, gáling lang nasayup ang miskla,</i> It
should have been good, only the mixture
was in the wrong proportions. <b>2</b> just, take
[so-and-so] rather than some other choice.
<b>2a</b> <i>with nominal predicate and verb subject:</i>
let [so-and-so] do it. <i>Aku lay dá áni bi,</i>
There, let me carry this. <i>Ikaw lay pangutána,</i>
You ask. (Lit. let you be the one to
ask.) <b>2a1</b> [<i>pronoun, noun</i>] -- [so-and-so]
will take the consequences. <i>Ug ímung buhátun,
ikaw lang,</i> If you do it, you take the
responsibility. <b>2b</b> <i>with quantities:</i> just make
it [so-and-so] much. <i>Trayinta lang ni ha?</i>
Can I have it for thirty? <b>2b1</b> <b>anhi, dinhi,</b>
-----File: 1162.png--------------------------------------------------------
<b>nganhi --</b> only up to here. <i>Anhi lang ku dinhi
manáug,</i> I'll just get off here. <b>2c</b> <i>with
verb:</i> take the choice of [do]ing. <i>Ang isdang
dílì mahálin gamsun lang, dílì bularun,</i>
If they can't sell the fish, they just salt it.
They don't dry it. <i>Ayaw lag anhi ugmà, kay
mahímu man sa Huybis,</i> Don't bother coming
tomorrow because you can do it on
Thursday. <b>sígi --</b> <b>2c1</b> never mind. <b>2c2</b> well,
all right, I'll agree to it. <i>Sígi lang. Dì lang ku
mudayug palit kay mahal,</i> Never mind. I
won't buy it because it's expensive. <i>Sígi
lang, itúgut ku na lang nig bayinti,</i> Oh, all
right. I'll let you have it for twenty centavos.
<b>ákù (íya, ímu) --</b> just let me (him) have
it rather than s.o. else. <i>Ákù lang ni. Kadtu
lay ihátag ni Pidru,</i> Let me have this one.
Just let Pedro have the other one. <b>2c3</b> can't
help [do]ing. <i>Mahadluk lang ta bisan sa
pagpanimátì lang,</i> We can't help getting
cold shivers, even just hearing about it. <b>2c4</b>
<b>mau --</b> <b>2c4a</b> it cannot be otherwise. <i>'Mu ba
siya ang nakaingun?'--'Mu lang!'</i> 'Is he the
one that caused it?'--'Of course! Who else
could it have been. <b>2c4b</b> yes, most certainly
so. <i>'Mukáun kag surbíti?'--'Káun mu lang,'</i>
'Would you like to eat ice cream?'--'I sure
would.' <b>3 na --</b> <b>3a</b> now it is only [so-and-so
much] where it was more before. <i>Sukad
sila namalhin aku na lang ang nahibilin,</i> After
they moved away I was the only one
left. <i>Human na ang tanan, paglimpiyu na
lang,</i> Everything is done. Only the cleaning
remains. <i>Duul na lang ang átung gidulngan,</i>
It is just a little way further to where we're
going. 3b just take [so-and-so] rather than
some other manifestly better choice. <b>3b1</b>
<i>with nominal predicate and verb subject:</i>
[so-and-so] will do it, though it should not
be so. <i>Aku na lay tiwas áni, kay madúgay ug
láing táwu,</i> Let me just do this myself because
it would take forever if s.o. else were
to do it. <b>3b2</b> <i>with quantities:</i> just make it
[so-and-so much] (which is less than what
one would ordinarily get). <i>Trayinta na lang
ni, ha?</i> Just let me have it for thirty, this
time, all right? <b>3b2a</b> <b>anhi --</b> just here (when
I really want to do it elsewhere). <i>Kay lisud
man ug musúd, anhi na lang ku sa iskína manáug,</i>
Since it's difficult to take a vehicle in,
I'll just get off at the corner. <b>3b3</b> [do] as
the best choice under the circumstances.
<i>Gamsa na lang nang isdáa kay wà nay mupalit,</i>
You might as well just salt that fish
because there isn't anybody who'll buy it.
<i>Ayaw na lag dad-a ug bug-atan ka,</i> Don't
bother taking it if you find it too heavy.
<b>sígi na --</b> = <sc>SÍGI LÁMANG</sc>. <b>ákù, íya na --</b> let
-----File: 1163.png--------------------------------------------------------
me (him) have it (although you might have
s.t. better to do with it). <i>Ákù na lang ni,
ha?</i> Let me have it, may I? <b>salámat na --</b>
I thank you, since I can't pay you any other
way. <i>Ug dì ka pabáyad, salámat na lang,</i>
Since you won't let me pay you, just let me
thank you. <b>3c</b> can't help [do]ing. <i>Sa tantung
kapungut nalímut na lang siya sa íyang
kaugalíngun,</i> He was so angry he just forgot
himself. <b>3c1</b> <i>following expressions referring
to time:</i> it's already [so-and-so] late and s.t.
still hasn't happened or hasn't stopped happening.
<i>Udtu na lang ug naglúkun lang gihápun
sa banig,</i> It's already noon, and he's
still curled up asleep. <i>Gabíi na lang wà gihápun
siya,</i> It's already night and he still has
not come home. <b>3c2</b> <b>dayag, kláru na --</b> obviously,
can't help being that way. <i>Kláru na
lang nga muhílak ug ímung kusiun,</i> Obviously
he's going to cry if you pinch him. <b>3c3</b>
<b>salámat na -- nga</b> the only saving grace was.
<i>Malumus untà ku. Salámat na lang nga dinhay
nakakità nákù,</i> I would have drowned,
but thank God, s.o. saw me. <b>4 pa --</b> <b>4a</b> <i>following
expression of time:</i> <b>4a1</b> [such-and-such]
was the first. <i>Karun pa lang ku makakità
sa ingun,</i> This is the very first time I
ever saw anything like that. <b>4a2</b> if it was so
at [such-and-such] a time already, it would
be even worse later. <i>Sa súgud pa lang nahanákan
na siya,</i> At the very beginning he was
already out of breath. <b>4a3</b> [so-and-so] just
happened now. <i>Karun pa lang siya muabut,</i>
He just arrived now. <i>Daw kagahápun pa
lang,</i> It seems like only yesterday. <b>4b</b> lest
[so-and-so] happen. <i>Dì ku mudúul sa irù
kay paákun pa lang ku,</i> I won't go near the
dog, because I might get bitten. <b>4c</b> if [so-and-so]
had been the case. <i>Dì pa lang ka
amígu nákù, ikíha ta ka,</i> If you were not my
friend, I would have filed a case against you.
<i>Aku pa lay gipabúhat, gwápu tag ági,</i> if
they had told me to do it, it would have
come out nice.

<b>lam-ang_1</b> <i>v</i> [A; b4] <b>1</b> overstep, go over s.t.
<i>Nalam-angan ku ang lítir dyi,</i> I skipped letter
g. <b>2</b> go beyond what is normally expected.
<i>Milam-ang sa maáyung pamatásan ang

has gone beyond the limits of good manners.
<i>Hilam-angan ra sad ang ímung pagkaáyu,</i>
Your goodness is far beyond what one
would expect. <i>a</i> taken beyond normal
bounds. <i>Lam-ang kaáyu ang íyang pagpangasábà,</i>
Her scolding has gone too far.

<b>lam-ang_2</b> <i>n</i> name of an Ilocano epic.

<b>lamánu</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AC; ab2] shake hands. <i>Naglamánu

One smile was enough to enchant him.
<i>Nalámat siya sa katahum sa kagabhíun,</i> He

<b>lámay_1</b> <i>v</i> [A; b] for a sickness, feeling, vice
-----File: 1165.png--------------------------------------------------------
to become deep-seated and take root or for

na ang ispiritu sa álak,</i> He loses his

<b>lámay_{2}</b> <i>v</i> [A; b(1)] join a @wake for the dead

<b>lamba</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; b5c] @slam s.t. long and hard
against s.t. <i>Kinsang pliyíra tung milamba sa
bátir sa yútà?</i> Who was that player who
swung the bat hard against the ground?
<i>Kupti ang h[=á]s sa íkug unyà ilamba sa paril,</i>
Hold the snake by the tail and swing it hard
against the stone wall. <i>Nalamba ang sakayan
ngadtu sa kabatuan,</i> The boat was slammed
against the rocks. <b>2</b> [A; b6(1)] pass a
basketball from a distance to one's teammate.
<i>Lambahi (lambáhi) tung kaúban nátung
way gwardiya,</i> Throw the ball to the
teammate that no one is covering. <b>lambalamba</b>
<i>v</i> [B5; c1] be repeatedly thrown or
struck against s.t. <i>Naglambalamba ang sira
sa bintánà sa kakusug sa hángin,</i> The window
shutters swung back and forth against
the sills with the force of the wind. <i>n</i> the
action of throwing or striking repeatedly.

<b>lambang</b> <i>v</i> [AC; ac] <b>1</b> @join two things, usually
live, to each other. <i>Nagkalambang ang duha
ka hiniktang sunuy nga gidúul paghigut,</i>
The two roosters that were tied too closely
to each other got entangled with one another.
<i>Lambánga ang duha ka karabaw,</i> Tie
the two carabaos together. <b>2</b> for animals to
have sexual intercourse, and, by coarse extension,
for people to do so. <i>Duha ka irù
nga naglambang,</i> Two dogs copulating. <i>À,
makiglambang lang nà bisag unsung bayhána,</i>
He doesn't care who he screws.

<b>lambanug, lambánug</b> <i>n</i> alcoholic drink made
from the water taken from the nipa palm
bud that has been fermented and distilled.

<b>lambáruk</b> <i>n</i> k.o. @mackerel (small <i>adlù</i>).

<b>lambay_{1}</b> = <sc>LANGBAY</sc>.

<b>*lambay_{2} -in-</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> k.o. @{stage play}, usually
about heroic deeds of past ages, with a dialogue
delivered in verse. <b>2</b> s.t. put on for the
show of it. <i>Kanang paggúkud kunúhay sa
mga dagkung ismaglir usa lang ka linambay,</i>

<b>langbay</b> <i>n</i> edible swimming crabs, found in
shallow and deep waters, rather similar in
shape and flavor to the blue crabs sold in
the States. They differ from other crabs in
that the shell has two sharp points on the
sides, both claws are the same size and only
slightly larger than the other limbs. Deep-sea
specimens may grow as big as a foot across.
<b>paN-</b> <i>v</i> [A2; b6] catch this sort of crab. <b>-an</b>,

<b>2</b> echo. <i>Walay mitubag gawas sa lánug

to more members of a group than should
have had it done to them. <i>Siyay naglapung
ug pangulitáwu sa tulu námù ka tindíra,</i> He
courted all the three of our salesgirls at one
time. <i>Makalapung kag dakup niánang mga
manúka?</i> Could you catch all those chickens
at one time? <i>Gilapung ku níyag áway
bísag wà ku makasâ,</i> She quarreled with
everyone, including me, even though I had
not done anything wrong. <i>Nalapung ang ámung
balay sa súnug,</i> Our house got burnt
along with the others.

<b>lapus</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A2; ac] @{penetrate}, @{pierce} through
the opposite side. <i>Dì makalapus ang ulan sa
atup,</i> The rain can't penetrate the roof. <i>Nalapsan
sa panà ang isdà,</i> The spear went
through the fish. <b>1a</b> [b4] have one's menstrual
blood penetrate to one's clothing.
<i>Gilapsan ku, maung mag-ílis ku,</i> I got men-*
-----File: 1200.png--------------------------------------------------------
*strual blood on my dress so I have to
change. <b>2</b> [A2; b6(1)] @{bypass}, pass through
or beyond a point. <i>Dì na ku mulapus ngadtu
sa píkas bungtud,</i> I won't go beyond the
other side of the hill. <b>2a</b> [A12; b6(1)] finish
one's studies. <i>Nakalapus na siya sa abugasíya,</i>
He has gotten through his law course.
<b>2b</b> [A2; a1c] go up to, reach. <i>Milapus ba
ning karsadáha ngadtu sa Lilúan?</i> Does this
road go all the way through to Liloan? <b>3</b> [C23; a12]
for two holes to lead through to
each other. <i>Ang duha ka lángub naglápus,</i>
The two caves lead into each other. <b>4</b> [B2]
for the foreskin of the penis to get loose so
that the glans can be exposed. <i>Magpatúlì ku
kun mulapus nag ákung tintin,</i> I'll get circumcised
when the foreskin of my thing is
loose enough to pull back all the way. <i>a</i> <b>1</b> be
finished with one's course of studies. <b>2</b> turn
out to be relatively more beautiful than the
others in a group. <i>Námung magsúun si Nína
ray lapus,</i> Nena is the only good-looking
one among us children. <b>(<-)</b> <i>a</i> going clear
through the other side. <i>Lápus ba ang lungag
sa masig ka dawunggan?</i> Do the earholes
go clear through the head to the other side?
<b>lapsanan</b> <i>n</i> place where s.t or s.o. exits[**missing .? P2]
<i>Dúna bay lapsanan ning pasilyúha?</i> Does
this passageway have an exit?

<b>laput</b> <i>n</i> term for various kinds of fry or tiny
fishes caught by the sanggab.

<b>láput</b> = <sc>LAP-UT_{2}</sc>.

<b>lap-ut_{1}</b> <i>v</i> [B126; b2] get slightly burnt, lightly
injured from heat or acid. <i>Nalap-ut ang
ákung tudlù sa asidu muryatiku,</i> My finger
got scalded with muriatic acid. <i>Nalap-ut
ákung bukubuku sa ínit,</i> My back got burnt
in the sun. <i>n</i> light burn.

<b>lap-ut_2</b> <i>a</i> for a liquid to get thick and sticky.
<i>v</i> [B3(1)] for soup to thicken. <i>Mulap-ut
ang sabaw sa útan nga sagúlan ug bisul,</i> Vegetable
soup thickens if yautia is stewed
with it. <i>Haúna sa dì pa makalap-ut,</i> Take it
out before it gets thick. <i>Ang harína nakalap-ut
(nakapalap-ut) sa sabaw,</i> The flour
made the soup too thick. <b>-ay</b>, <b>-ay(->)</b> =
<sc>LAP-UT</sc>.

<b>lapuy</b> <i>v</i> [B; a4b4] be @{weary}, @{fatigued}. <i>Nalapuy
(milapuy) ang ákung mga buktun sa
pagginúna,</i> My arms have become fatigued
from weeding. <i>Gilapuy (gilapuyan) kug maáyu
sa paglinanguy,</i> I was exhausted from
swimming so much. <i>a</i> @{fatigued}. <b>ka-</b> <i>n</i> body
fatigue.

<b>lapwa</b> <i>v</i> [A; b6(1)] put s.t. in boiling water,
to blanch, sterilize, or prepare it for further
cooking. <i>Lapwái (lapwáhi) ang kutsára
sa masakitun,</i> Sterilize the patient's spoon
